"C:\\Windows\\System32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\powershell.exe" -Command "Get-Content 'functions/src/generate_wa_me_link.ts' | Select-Object -First 260" in C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project
 succeeded in 283ms:
// =============================================================================
// generateWaMeLink â€” I6.5 companion, WhatsApp deep-link generator.
//
// HTTPS Callable (onCall). Reads the shop's WhatsApp number from the theme
// document and constructs a wa.me deep link with an optional pre-filled
// Hindi message template including the project ID.
//
// Input: { shopId, projectId, messageText? }
// Returns: { url: string }
// =============================================================================

import * as admin from 'firebase-admin';
import { onCall, HttpsError } from 'firebase-functions/v2/https';
import { logger } from 'firebase-functions/v2';

import { mintJoinToken } from './lib/hmac_join_token';

/// Default Hindi message template. The {projectId} placeholder is replaced
/// at runtime. This is the greeting a customer sees pre-filled in WhatsApp
/// when they tap "Chat on WhatsApp" from the app.
const DEFAULT_MESSAGE_TEMPLATE =
  'Namaste! Mujhe Project #{projectId} ke baare mein baat karni hai.';

/// Per-shop subdomain pattern used in the join deep link
/// (https://{shopId}.yugmalabs.ai/join?token=...). The marketing site
/// catches `/join?token=...` and forwards into the customer app via
/// Android App Links / iOS Universal Links â€” Phase 1 multi-tenant work
/// per docs/architecture-source-of-truth.md Â§15. Until that infra ships,
/// the URL still goes out and is signature-verifiable; the recipient
/// just sees the marketing site instead of the app.
const JOIN_DEEP_LINK_HOST_TEMPLATE = 'https://{shopId}.yugmalabs.ai/join';

interface GenerateWaMeLinkRequest {
  shopId: string;
  projectId: string;
  messageText?: string;
  /**
   * Opt-in flag â€” when `true`, the response wa.me text includes a
   * Decision-Circle join deep link signed with an HMAC-SHA256 token (ADR-009
   * v1.0.3 / drift Â§15.1.A). The token's `originalCustomerUid` is the
   * caller's `request.auth.uid` â€” never trust a caller-supplied value.
   */
  includeJoinLink?: boolean;
}

export const generateWaMeLink = onCall(
  {
    region: 'asia-south1',
    memory: '256MiB',
    timeoutSeconds: 30,
    // Â§15.1.C â€” server-side App Check enforcement. Rejects calls that
    // arrive without a valid App Check token; prevents cross-tenant
    // phone number disclosure via unattested clients.
    enforceAppCheck: true,
    // Â§15.1.A â€” HMAC join token signing. Wired via Firebase Secret
    // Manager: set with `firebase functions:secrets:set
    // JOIN_TOKEN_HMAC_SECRET` per docs/runbook/staging-setup.md.
    secrets: ['JOIN_TOKEN_HMAC_SECRET'],
  },
  async (request) => {
    // â”€â”€ Auth check â”€â”€
    if (!request.auth) {
      throw new HttpsError('unauthenticated', 'Authentication required.');
    }

    const data = request.data as GenerateWaMeLinkRequest;

    // â”€â”€ Input validation â”€â”€
    if (!data.shopId || typeof data.shopId !== 'string') {
      throw new HttpsError('invalid-argument', 'shopId is required.');
    }
    if (!data.projectId || typeof data.projectId !== 'string') {
      throw new HttpsError('invalid-argument', 'projectId is required.');
    }

    const { shopId, projectId } = data;

    // BE001 fix: validate caller's shopId token matches the provided shopId.
    // Prevents cross-tenant phone number disclosure.
    const callerShopId = request.auth.token?.shopId;
    if (callerShopId !== shopId) {
      throw new HttpsError(
        'permission-denied',
        'Shop mismatch: caller does not belong to this shop.',
      );
    }

    const db = admin.firestore();

    // Read shop's WhatsApp number from theme document.
    const themeRef = db
      .collection('shops')
      .doc(shopId)
      .collection('theme')
      .doc('current');
    const themeSnap = await themeRef.get();

    if (!themeSnap.exists) {
      throw new HttpsError(
        'not-found',
        `Theme document not found for shop '${shopId}'.`,
      );
    }

    const themeData = themeSnap.data();
    const whatsappNumberE164 = themeData?.whatsappNumberE164;

    if (!whatsappNumberE164 || typeof whatsappNumberE164 !== 'string') {
      throw new HttpsError(
        'failed-precondition',
        `Shop '${shopId}' does not have a WhatsApp number configured.`,
      );
    }

    // Strip the leading '+' for wa.me URL format.
    const phone = whatsappNumberE164.replace(/^\+/, '');

    // Build the message text.
    let messageText =
      data.messageText && typeof data.messageText === 'string'
        ? data.messageText
        : DEFAULT_MESSAGE_TEMPLATE.replace('{projectId}', projectId);

    // Â§15.1.A â€” append a signed Decision-Circle join deep link if the
    // caller asked for one. The token binds {shopId, projectId,
    // originalCustomerUid: callerUid, expiresAt: now+7d} and is verified
    // by `joinDecisionCircle` before the actual merge. The caller's
    // `originalCustomerUid` is the auth.uid â€” caller-supplied UIDs are
    // ignored to prevent spoofing.
    if (data.includeJoinLink === true) {
      const joinToken = mintJoinToken({
        shopId,
        projectId,
        originalCustomerUid: request.auth.uid,
      });
      // DNS labels must not contain underscores â€” replace with hyphens so
      // synthetic IDs like shop_0 / shop_1 produce valid hostnames.
      const dnsShopId = shopId.replace(/_/g, '-');
      const joinUrl =
        JOIN_DEEP_LINK_HOST_TEMPLATE.replace('{shopId}', dnsShopId) +
        `?token=${encodeURIComponent(joinToken)}`;
      messageText = `${messageText}\n\n${joinUrl}`;
    }

    const url = `https://wa.me/${phone}?text=${encodeURIComponent(messageText)}`;

    logger.info('generateWaMeLink: link generated', {
      shopId,
      projectId,
      callerUid: request.auth.uid,
      includeJoinLink: data.includeJoinLink === true,
    });

    return { url };
  },
);

// **************************************************************************
// JsonSerializableGenerator
// **************************************************************************

_$CustomerMemoryImpl _$$CustomerMemoryImplFromJson(Map<String, dynamic> json) =>
    _$CustomerMemoryImpl(
      customerUid: json['customerUid'] as String,
      shopId: json['shopId'] as String,
      notes: json['notes'] as String? ?? '',
      relationshipNotes: json['relationshipNotes'] as String? ?? '',
      preferredOccasions: (json['preferredOccasions'] as List<dynamic>?)
              ?.map((e) => $enumDecode(_$PreferredOccasionEnumMap, e,
                  unknownValue: PreferredOccasion.other))
              .toList() ??
          const <PreferredOccasion>[],
      preferredPriceMin: (json['preferredPriceMin'] as num?)?.toInt(),
      preferredPriceMax: (json['preferredPriceMax'] as num?)?.toInt(),
      firstSeenAt: json['firstSeenAt'] == null
          ? null
          : DateTime.parse(json['firstSeenAt'] as String),
      lastSeenAt: json['lastSeenAt'] == null
          ? null
          : DateTime.parse(json['lastSeenAt'] as String),
      totalProjectsLifetime:
          (json['totalProjectsLifetime'] as num?)?.toInt() ?? 0,
    );

Map<String, dynamic> _$$CustomerMemoryImplToJson(
        _$CustomerMemoryImpl instance) =>
    <String, dynamic>{
      'customerUid': instance.customerUid,
      'shopId': instance.shopId,
      'notes': instance.notes,
      'relationshipNotes': instance.relationshipNotes,
      'preferredOccasions': instance.preferredOccasions
          .map((e) => _$PreferredOccasionEnumMap[e]!)
          .toList(),
      'preferredPriceMin': instance.preferredPriceMin,
      'preferredPriceMax': instance.preferredPriceMax,
      'firstSeenAt': instance.firstSeenAt?.toIso8601String(),
      'lastSeenAt': instance.lastSeenAt?.toIso8601String(),
      'totalProjectsLifetime': instance.totalProjectsLifetime,
    };

const _$PreferredOccasionEnumMap = {
  PreferredOccasion.shaadi: 'shaadi',
  PreferredOccasion.nayaGhar: 'nayaGhar',
  PreferredOccasion.betiKaGhar: 'beti_ka_ghar',
  PreferredOccasion.puranaBadalne: 'puranaBadalne',
  PreferredOccasion.budget: 'budget',
  PreferredOccasion.ladies: 'ladies',
  PreferredOccasion.other: 'other',
};

652-```
653-
654-**Critical properties:**
--
656-1. **Husband does NOT need to verify his phone.** Anonymous Auth is sufficient for participation. He only needs to phone-verify if HE personally commits to a separate Project of his own. His participation in the wife's Project is read+write but not commit-authoritative — only the original `customerUid` (uid_A) can transition the Project to `committed` state. The wife is the contractual customer of record; the husband is a participating viewer/discusser.
657-
658-2. **Join tokens are signed and time-limited.** The `generateWaMeLink` Cloud Function (SAD §7 Function 2) is extended to also produce a join token: an HMAC-SHA256 signature over `{shopId, projectId, originalCustomerUid, expiresAt}` using a server-side secret stored in Firebase Functions config. The token expires after 7 days. Tampered or expired tokens are rejected with `permission-denied`.
659-
660:3. **The `joinDecisionCircle` Cloud Function** (added to SAD §7 inventory as Function #6 — see below) is an HTTPS callable that takes the join token + the joining user's anonymous UID, validates the token, and atomically writes to both the chat thread's `participantUids` array and the Decision Circle document's `participants` array (if Decision Circle is enabled per the `decisionCircleEnabled` Remote Config flag).
661-
662-4. **Cross-tenant integrity:** the Cloud Function asserts `joiningUid`'s `request.auth.uid` matches the function caller, and the join token's `shopId` matches the chat thread's `shopId`. A husband cannot use a token for shop_A to join a thread in shop_B.
663-
664:5. **Read access enforcement:** §6 security rules (post-v1.0.2 patch) check `request.auth.uid in resource.data.participantUids` for chat thread reads. Once `joinDecisionCircle` writes the husband's UID to the array, the security rules grant him read access automatically.
665-
666-6. **The husband does NOT see the wife's customer_memory document** — that remains operator-only per the original §5 schema and §6 rule. Customer memory is the shopkeeper's private notes, not part of the Decision Circle shared state.
667-
668-This flow closes the architectural gap that Sally and the frontend-design plugin both flagged independently. It is a v1 implementation requirement, not v1.5 polish.
--
987-  shopId: "sunil-trading-company",
988-  projectId: "proj_<ulid>",
989-  customerUid: "<uid>",                      // primary thread owner (the
990-                                              // anonymous UID that started the Project)
991:  // v1.0.2 patch: participantUids supports Decision Circle multi-device.
992-  // When a husband on a separate phone joins via a wa.me deep link, his
993-  // anonymous UID is appended here, granting him read+write access to
994-  // this thread without becoming the customerUid. Operators are NOT in
995-  // this array — they're authenticated via isOperatorOf(shopId) instead.
996:  participantUids: ["<customerUid>", "<husband-anon-uid>", "<bhabhi-anon-uid>"],
997-  messageCount: 12,                          // denormalized
998-  lastMessagePreview: "Polish kab?",
999-  lastMessageAt: <timestamp>,
1000-  // Messages in: shops/{shopId}/chat_threads/{projectId}/messages/{messageId}
1001-}
1002-```
1003-
1004:**Adding participants to a chat thread:** the customer who originally created the Project (and thus the chat thread) can add additional anonymous UIDs to `participantUids` via a `joinDecisionCircle()` Cloud Function call, triggered when another family member opens a `wa.me` deep link the original customer shared. The Cloud Function validates that the joining session has read access to the deep link's referenced Project, then appends the joining UID. This is the canonical "Decision Circle multi-device join" auth flow that SAD §4 originally did not specify — added in v1.0.2 patch per Sally and frontend-design plugin pushback.
1005-
1006-**Message** (sub-sub-collection)
1007-```typescript
1008-// shops/{shopId}/chat_threads/{projectId}/messages/{messageId}
--

1428-
1429-    match /shops/{shopId}/chat_threads/{threadId} {
1430-      // v1.0.2 patch: chat threads now support Decision Circle multi-device
1431:      // participants via the participantUids[] array. The original
1432-      // customerUid is the thread owner; additional participants (e.g.,

2060-
2061:### Function 6: `joinDecisionCircle` (v1.0.3 patch — added per SAD §4 Flow 5)
2062-
2063-**Trigger:** HTTPS callable
2064-**Runtime:** Node 22 LTS, 256 MB memory, 30s timeout
2065:**Purpose:** Validate a join token from a `wa.me` deep link and atomically add the joining customer's anonymous UID to the chat thread's `participantUids[]` array (and the Decision Circle document's `participants[]` array if Decision Circle is enabled). Per SAD §4 Flow 5, this is the canonical "Decision Circle multi-device join" auth flow.

codex
The new token-based Decision Circle flow introduces a same-shop authorization bypass and also replaces, rather than adds, participants on successful joins. Those issues break the intended share-link behavior and should be fixed before considering the patch correct.

Full review comments:

- [P1] Reject token joins unless `sourceUid` already owns the thread — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\functions\src\join_decision_circle.ts:300-306
  When `joinToken` is present, this path fetches `chatThreads/{projectId}` and updates it without verifying that the thread actually belongs to `sourceUid` (for example `customerUid == sourceUid` or `participantUids` already contains `sourceUid`). Because `generateWaMeLink` now mints a valid token for any `projectId` in the caller's shop, a malicious customer who can guess another project's ID can add arbitrary `destUid`s to that victim thread and gain chat access cross-customer within the same shop.

- [P1] Preserve the original customer in token-based participant joins — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\functions\src\join_decision_circle.ts:284-287
  The new token flow is documented as a participant add, but `updateThread()` still rewrites `participantUids` as `currentParticipants - sourceUid + destUid`. In a normal share-link join, that removes the original customer from the chat thread as soon as the family member joins, so the source customer loses chat access even though `project.customerUid` is intentionally left unchanged.
The new token-based Decision Circle flow introduces a same-shop authorization bypass and also replaces, rather than adds, participants on successful joins. Those issues break the intended share-link behavior and should be fixed before considering the patch correct.

Full review comments:

- [P1] Reject token joins unless `sourceUid` already owns the thread — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\functions\src\join_decision_circle.ts:300-306
  When `joinToken` is present, this path fetches `chatThreads/{projectId}` and updates it without verifying that the thread actually belongs to `sourceUid` (for example `customerUid == sourceUid` or `participantUids` already contains `sourceUid`). Because `generateWaMeLink` now mints a valid token for any `projectId` in the caller's shop, a malicious customer who can guess another project's ID can add arbitrary `destUid`s to that victim thread and gain chat access cross-customer within the same shop.

- [P1] Preserve the original customer in token-based participant joins — C:\Alok\Business Projects\Almira-Project\functions\src\join_decision_circle.ts:284-287
  The new token flow is documented as a participant add, but `updateThread()` still rewrites `participantUids` as `currentParticipants - sourceUid + destUid`. In a normal share-link join, that removes the original customer from the chat thread as soon as the family member joins, so the source customer loses chat access even though `project.customerUid` is intentionally left unchanged.
